    70	func newImageResource(img *images.Image, base baseResource) *imageResource {
    71	        ir := &imageResource{
    72	                Image:        img,
    73	                baseResource: base,
    74	        }
    75	        ir.root = ir
    76	        ir.exifInfoFn = ir.newExifInfoFn()
    77	        ir.metaInfoFn = ir.newMetaInfoFn()
    78	        ir.colorsFn = ir.newColorsFn()
    79	        return ir
    80	}
    81	
    82	func (i *imageResource) newExifInfoFn() func() (*meta.ExifInfo, error) {
    83	        return sync.OnceValues(func() (*meta.ExifInfo, error) {
    84	                hugo.Deprecate("Image.Exif", "Use Image.Meta, see https://gohugo.io/content-management/image-processing/#meta", "v0.155.0")
    85	                mf := i.Format.ToImageMetaImageFormatFormat()
    86	                if mf == -1 {
    87	                        return nil, nil
    88	                }
    89	
    90	                var result *meta.ExifInfo
    91	                key := i.getImageMetaCacheTargetPath()
    92	
    93	                read := func(info filecache.ItemInfo, r io.ReadSeeker) error {
    94	                        data, err := io.ReadAll(r)
    95	                        if err != nil {
    96	                                return err
    97	                        }
    98	                        return json.Unmarshal(data, &result)
    99	                }
   100	
   101	                create := func(info filecache.ItemInfo, w io.WriteCloser) (err error) {
   102	                        defer w.Close()
   103	                        f, err := i.ReadSeekCloser()
   104	                        if err != nil {
   105	                                return err
   106	                        }
   107	                        defer f.Close()
   108	
   109	                        filename := InternalResourceSourcePathBestEffort(i)
   110	                        result, err = i.getSpec().Imaging.DecodeExif(filename, mf, f)
   111	                        if err != nil {
   112	                                i.getSpec().Logger.Warnf("Unable to decode Exif metadata from image: %s", i.Key())
   113	                                return nil
   114	                        }
   115	
   116	                        enc := json.NewEncoder(w)
   117	                        return enc.Encode(result)
   118	                }
   119	
   120	                _, err := i.getSpec().ImageCache.fcache.ReadOrCreate(key, read, create)
   121	                return result, err
   122	        })
   123	}
   124

   167	func (i *imageResource) newColorsFn() func() ([]images.Color, error) {
   168	        return sync.OnceValues(func() ([]images.Color, error) {
   169	                img, err := i.DecodeImage()
   170	                if err != nil {
   171	                        return nil, err
   172	                }
   173	                colors := color_extractor.ExtractColors(img)
   174	                result := make([]images.Color, len(colors))
   175	                for j, c := range colors {
   176	                        result[j] = images.ColorGoToColor(c)
   177	                }
   178	                return result, nil
   179	        })
   180	}

   182	func (i *imageResource) Exif() *meta.ExifInfo {
   183	        x, err := i.root.exifInfoFn()
   184	        if err != nil {
   185	                panic(fmt.Sprintf("exif init failed: %s", err))
   186	        }
   187	        return x
   188	}

   191	        m, err := i.root.metaInfoFn()
   192	        if err != nil {

   198	func (i *imageResource) getImageMetaInfoCacheTargetPath() string {
   199	        // Increment to invalidate the meta cache
   200	        const imageMetaInfoVersionNumber = 1
   201	
   202	        cfgHash := i.getSpec().Imaging.Cfg.SourceHash
   203	        df := i.getResourcePaths()
   204	        p1, _ := paths.FileAndExt(df.File)
   205	        h := i.hash()
   206	        idStr := hashing.HashStringHex(h, i.size(), imageMetaInfoVersionNumber, cfgHash)
   207	        df.File = fmt.Sprintf("%s_%s_meta.json", p1, idStr)

   222	func (i *imageResource) Clone() resource.Resource {
   223	        gr := i.baseResource.Clone().(baseResource)
   224	        ir := &imageResource{
   225	                root:         i.root,
   226	                Image:        i.WithSpec(gr),
   227	                baseResource: gr,
   228	        }
   229	        ir.colorsFn = ir.newColorsFn()
   230	        return ir
   231	}

   234	        gr := i.baseResource.cloneTo(targetPath).(baseResource)
   235	        ir := &imageResource{
   236	                root:         i.root,
   237	                Image:        i.WithSpec(gr),

   243	
   244	func (i *imageResource) cloneWithUpdates(u *transformationUpdate) (baseResource, error) {
   245	        base, err := i.baseResource.cloneWithUpdates(u)
   246	        if err != nil {
   247	                return nil, err
   248	        }
   249	
   250	        var img *images.Image
   251	
   252	        if u.isContentChanged() {
   253	                img = i.WithSpec(base)
   254	        } else {
   255	                img = i.Image
   256	        }
   257	
   258	        ir := &imageResource{
   259	                root:         i.root,
   260	                Image:        img,
   261	                baseResource: base,
   262	        }
   263	        ir.colorsFn = ir.newColorsFn()
   264	        return ir, nil
   265	}
   266	
   267	// Process processes the image with the given spec.
   268	// The spec can contain an optional action, one of "resize", "crop", "fit" or "fill".
   269	// This makes this method a more flexible version that covers all of Resize, Crop, Fit and Fill,
   270	// but it also supports e.g. format conversions without any resize action.
   271	func (i *imageResource) Process(spec string) (images.ImageResource, error) {
   272	        return i.processActionSpec("", spec)
   273	}
   274	
   275	// Resize resizes the image to the specified width and height using the specified resampling
   276	// filter and returns the transformed image. If one of width or height is 0, the image aspect
   277	// ratio is preserved.
   278	func (i *imageResource) Resize(spec string) (images.ImageResource, error) {
   279	        return i.processActionSpec(images.ActionResize, spec)
   280	}
   281	
   282	// Crop the image to the specified dimensions without resizing using the given anchor point.
   283	// Space delimited config, e.g. `200x300 TopLeft`.
   284	func (i *imageResource) Crop(spec string) (images.ImageResource, error) {
   285	        return i.processActionSpec(images.ActionCrop, spec)
   286	}
   287	
   288	// Fit scales down the image using the specified resample filter to fit the specified
   289	// maximum width and height.
   290	func (i *imageResource) Fit(spec string) (images.ImageResource, error) {
   291	        return i.processActionSpec(images.ActionFit, spec)
   292	}
   293	
   294	// Fill scales the image to the smallest possible size that will cover the specified dimensions,
   295	// crops the resized image to the specified dimensions using the given anchor point.
   296	// Space delimited config, e.g. `200x300 TopLeft`.
   297	func (i *imageResource) Fill(spec string) (images.ImageResource, error) {
   298	        return i.processActionSpec(images.ActionFill, spec)
   299	}
   300	
   301	func (i *imageResource) Filter(filters ...any) (images.ImageResource, error) {
   302	        var confMain images.ImageConfig
   303	
   304	        var gfilters []gift.Filter
   305	
   306	        for _, f := range filters {
   307	                gfilters = append(gfilters, images.ToFilters(f)...)
   308	        }
   309	
   310	        var options []string
   311	
   312	        for _, f := range gfilters {
   313	                f = images.UnwrapFilter(f)
   314	                if specProvider, ok := f.(images.ImageProcessSpecProvider); ok {
   315	                        options = append(options, strings.Fields(specProvider.ImageProcessSpec())...)
   316	                }
   317	        }
   318	
   319	        confMain, err := images.DecodeImageConfig(options, i.Proc.Cfg, i.Format)
   320	        if err != nil {
   321	                return nil, err
   322	        }
   323	
   324	        confMain.Action = "filter"
   325	        confMain.Key = hashing.HashString(gfilters)
   326	
   327	        return i.doWithImageConfig(confMain, func(src image.Image) (image.Image, error) {
   328	                var filters []gift.Filter
   329	                for _, f := range gfilters {
   330	                        f = images.UnwrapFilter(f)
   331	                        if specProvider, ok := f.(images.ImageProcessSpecProvider); ok {
   332	                                options := strings.Fields(specProvider.ImageProcessSpec())
   333	                                conf, err := images.DecodeImageConfig(options, i.Proc.Cfg, i.Format)
   334	                                if err != nil {
   335	                                        return nil, err
   336	                                }
   337	                                pFilters, err := i.Proc.FiltersFromConfig(src, conf)
   338	                                if err != nil {
   339	                                        return nil, err
   340	                                }
   341	                                filters = append(filters, pFilters...)
   342	                        } else if orientationProvider, ok := f.(images.ImageFilterFromOrientationProvider); ok {
   343	                                var orientation int
   344	                                if meta := i.Meta(); meta != nil {
   345	                                        orientation = meta.Orientation
   346	                                }
   347	                                if tf := orientationProvider.AutoOrient(orientation); tf != nil {
   348	                                        filters = append(filters, tf)
   349	                                }
   350	                        } else {
   351	                                filters = append(filters, f)
   352	                        }
   353	                }
   354	                return i.Proc.Filter(src, filters...)
   355	        })
   356	}
   357	
   358	func (i *imageResource) processActionSpec(action, spec string) (images.ImageResource, error) {
   359	        options := append([]string{action}, strings.Fields(strings.ToLower(spec))...)
   360	        ir, err := i.processOptions(options)
   361	        if err != nil {
   362	                if sourcePath := i.sourcePath(); sourcePath != "" {
   363	                        err = fmt.Errorf("failed to %s image %q: %w", action, sourcePath, err)
   364	                }
   365	                return nil, err
   366	        }
   367	        return ir, nil
   368	}
   369	
   370	func (i *imageResource) processOptions(options []string) (images.ImageResource, error) {
   371	        conf, err := images.DecodeImageConfig(options, i.Proc.Cfg, i.Format)
   372	        if err != nil {
   373	                return nil, err
   374	        }
   375	
   376	        img, err := i.doWithImageConfig(conf, func(src image.Image) (image.Image, error) {
   377	                return i.Proc.ApplyFiltersFromConfig(src, conf)
   378	        })
   379	        if err != nil {
   380	                return nil, err
   381	        }
   382	
   383	        if conf.Action == images.ActionFill {
   384	                if conf.Anchor == images.SmartCropAnchor && img.Width() == 0 || img.Height() == 0 {
   385	                        // See https://github.com/gohugoio/hugo/issues/7955
   386	                        // Smartcrop fails silently in some rare cases.
   387	                        // Fall back to a center fill.
   388	                        conf = conf.Reanchor(gift.CenterAnchor)
   389	                        return i.doWithImageConfig(conf, func(src image.Image) (image.Image, error) {
   390	                                return i.Proc.ApplyFiltersFromConfig(src, conf)
   391	                        })
   392	                }
   393	        }
   394	
   395	        return img, nil
   396	}
   397	
   398	var imageProcSem chan bool
   399	
   400	func init() {
   401	        imageProcWorkers := 1
   402	        if n := config.GetNumWorkerMultiplier(); n > 4 {
   403	                imageProcWorkers = 2
   404	        }
   405	        imageProcSem = make(chan bool, imageProcWorkers)
   406	}
   407	
   408	func (i *imageResource) doWithImageConfig(conf images.ImageConfig, f func(src image.Image) (image.Image, error)) (images.ImageResource, error) {
   409	        img, err := i.getSpec().ImageCache.getOrCreate(i, conf, func() (*imageResource, image.Image, error) {
   410	                imageProcSem <- true
   411	                defer func() {
   412	                        <-imageProcSem
   413	                }()
   414	
   415	                src, err := i.DecodeImage()
   416	                if err != nil {
   417	                        return nil, nil, &os.PathError{Op: conf.Action, Path: i.TargetPath(), Err: err}
   418	                }
   419	
   420	                converted, err := f(src)
   421	                if err != nil {
   422	                        return nil, nil, &os.PathError{Op: conf.Action, Path: i.TargetPath(), Err: err}
   423	                }
   424	
   425	                hasAlpha := !images.IsOpaque(converted)
   426	                shouldFill := conf.BgColor != nil && hasAlpha
   427	                shouldFill = shouldFill || (!conf.TargetFormat.SupportsTransparency() && hasAlpha)
   428	                var bgColor color.Color
   429	
   430	                if shouldFill {
   431	                        bgColor = conf.BgColor
   432	                        if bgColor == nil {
   433	                                bgColor = i.Proc.Cfg.Config.BgColor
   434	                        }
   435	                        tmp := image.NewRGBA(converted.Bounds())
   436	                        draw.Draw(tmp, tmp.Bounds(), image.NewUniform(bgColor), image.Point{}, draw.Src)
   437	                        draw.Draw(tmp, tmp.Bounds(), converted, converted.Bounds().Min, draw.Over)
   438	                        converted = tmp
   439	                }
   440	
   441	                if conf.TargetFormat == images.PNG {
   442	                        // Apply the colour palette from the source
   443	                        if paletted, ok := src.(*image.Paletted); ok {
   444	                                palette := paletted.Palette
   445	                                if bgColor != nil && len(palette) < 256 {
   446	                                        palette = images.AddColorToPalette(bgColor, palette)
   447	                                } else if bgColor != nil {
   448	                                        images.ReplaceColorInPalette(bgColor, palette)
   449	                                }
   450	                                tmp := image.NewPaletted(converted.Bounds(), palette)
   451	                                draw.FloydSteinberg.Draw(tmp, tmp.Bounds(), converted, converted.Bounds().Min)
   452	                                converted = tmp
   453	                        }
   454	                }
   455	
   456	                ci := i.clone(converted)
   457	                targetPath := i.relTargetPathFromConfig(conf, i.getSpec().Imaging.Cfg.SourceHash)
   458	                ci.setTargetPath(targetPath)
   459	                ci.Format = conf.TargetFormat
   460	                ci.setMediaType(conf.TargetFormat.MediaType())
   461	
   462	                return ci, converted, nil
   463	        })
   464	        if err != nil {
   465	                return nil, err
   466	        }
   467	        return img, nil
   468	}
   469	
   470	// DecodeImage decodes the image source into an Image.
   471	// This for internal use only.
   472	func (i *imageResource) DecodeImage() (image.Image, error) {
   473	        f, err := i.ReadSeekCloser()
   474	        if err != nil {
   475	                return nil, fmt.Errorf("failed to open image for decode: %w", err)
   476	        }
   477	        defer f.Close()
   478	
   479	        return i.getSpec().Imaging.Codec.DecodeFormat(i.Format, f)
   480	}
   481	
   482	func (i *imageResource) clone(img image.Image) *imageResource {
   483	        spec := i.baseResource.Clone().(baseResource)
   484	
   485	        var image *images.Image
   486	        if img != nil {
   487	                image = i.WithImage(img)
   488	        } else {
   489	                image = i.WithSpec(spec)
   490	        }
   491	
   492	        ir := &imageResource{
   493	                Image:        image,
   494	                root:         i.root,
   495	                baseResource: spec,
   496	        }
   497	        ir.colorsFn = ir.newColorsFn()
   498	        return ir
   499	}
   500	
   501	func (i *imageResource) getImageMetaCacheTargetPath() string {
   502	        // Increment to invalidate the meta cache
   503	        // Last increment: v0.130.0 when change to the new imagemeta library for Exif.
   504	        const imageMetaVersionNumber = 2
   505	
   506	        cfgHash := i.getSpec().Imaging.Cfg.SourceHash
   507	        df := i.getResourcePaths()
   508	        p1, _ := paths.FileAndExt(df.File)
   509	        h := i.hash()
   510	        idStr := hashing.HashStringHex(h, i.size(), imageMetaVersionNumber, cfgHash)
   511	        df.File = fmt.Sprintf("%s_%s.json", p1, idStr)
   512	        return df.TargetPath()
   513	}
   514	
   515	func (i *imageResource) relTargetPathFromConfig(conf images.ImageConfig, imagingConfigSourceHash string) internal.ResourcePaths {
   516	        p1, p2 := paths.FileAndExt(i.getResourcePaths().File)
   517	        if conf.TargetFormat != i.Format {
   518	                p2 = conf.TargetFormat.DefaultExtension()
   519	        }
   520	
   521	        // Do not change.
   522	        const imageHashPrefix = "_hu_"
   523	
   524	        huIdx := strings.LastIndex(p1, imageHashPrefix)
   525	        incomingID := ""
   526	        if huIdx > -1 {
   527	                incomingID = p1[huIdx+len(imageHashPrefix):]
   528	                p1 = p1[:huIdx]
   529	        }
   530	
   531	        hash := hashing.HashStringHex(incomingID, i.hash(), conf.Key, imagingConfigSourceHash)
   532	        rp := i.getResourcePaths()
   533	        rp.File = fmt.Sprintf("%s%s%s%s", p1, imageHashPrefix, hash, p2)
   534	
   535	        return rp
   536	}

2026-05-29 21:48:21,143 - INFO - swea-agent-gohugoio__hugo-14685 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I need to understand the key issue. Let me look at `NewOpenReadSeekCloser` more carefully:

```go
func NewOpenReadSeekCloser(r ReadSeekCloser) OpenReadSeekCloser {
    return func() (ReadSeekCloser, error) {
        r.Seek(0, io.SeekStart)
        return r, nil
    }
}
```

This returns a closure that captures `r` by reference. Each time it's called, it seeks the SAME `r` back to start and returns it. If two goroutines call this function simultaneously:

1. Goroutine A calls `OpenReadSeekCloser()`, gets the reader
2. Goroutine B calls `OpenReadSeekCloser()`, calls `r.Seek(0, io.SeekStart)` while A is reading
3. Goroutine A now reads corrupted data

This is a classic race condition! The `ReadSeekCloser` is shared by reference.

But wait, let me check if this is actually the case for the specific scenario. The `ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser()` is called once when the resource source descriptor is created in `content_map_page_assembler.go`. The resulting `OpenReadSeekCloser` is stored in `rd.OpenReadSeekCloser`. Then `NewResource` stores it in `gr.sd.OpenReadSeekCloser`.

Each time someone calls `ReadSeekCloser()` on the resource, it calls `l.sd.OpenReadSeekCloser()`, which triggers the closure, which seeks the shared reader to 0 and returns it. If the resource is used concurrently (e.g., for hashing, for content rendering, for resize), this could cause the race.

But wait, there's another issue. Let me look at `hashImage`:

```go
func (r *resourceHash) init(l hugio.ReadSeekCloserProvider) error {
    var initErr error
    r.initOnce.Do(func() {
        var hash uint64
        var size int64
        f, err := l.ReadSeekCloser()
        if err != nil {
            initErr = fmt.Errorf("failed to open source: %w", err)
            return
        }
        defer f.Close()
        hash, size, err = hashImage(f)
        ...
    })
    return initErr
}
```

This calls `ReadSeekCloser()` which creates a new reader from the `OpenReadSeekCloser` closure. The `sync.Once` ensures this is only done once per `resourceHash` instance. But if the resource is cloned (for different sites), each clone gets its own `resourceHash` and would try to hash again.

> But the image is not corrupt in any way (views fine in any app, exiftool likes it, ImageMagick has no complaints, etc.).
> In some cases I had to run this command 20 times to trigger the error

This is clearly a race condition. Let me look at how resources from content adapters are handled when there are multiple sites/languages.

    r.r = nil

```

And how it's used in `content_map_page_assembler.go`:

Each clone will then create its own `resource.Resource` via `NewResource`. But the `rc` (ResourceConfig) is shared among clones! And `rc.Content.ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser()` returns the same closure that captures the same `ReadSeekCloser`.

```

And `filename` is:
```go
var filename string
if rs.fi != nil {
    filename = rs.fi.Meta().Filename
}
```

So the source filename comes from `rs.fi` which is `pt.GoTmplFi` - the template file! So the error message showing `_content.gotmpl` is just the source filename for error reporting, not the actual image data source.

OK, let me now focus on finding the actual race condition. Let me look at the `PagesFromTemplate` and how it's cloned for different sites:

In `content_map.go`:
```go
clone := contentAdapter.CloneForSite(ss)
```

And:
```go
func (p PagesFromTemplate) CloneForSite(s page.Site) *PagesFromTemplate {
    p.PagesFromTemplateOptions.Site = s
    p.PagesFromTemplateDeps = p.PagesFromTemplateOptions.DepsFromSite(s)
    p.buildState = &BuildState{
        sourceInfosCurrent: hmaps.NewCache[string, *sourceInfo](),
    }
    return &p
}
```

Note that `CloneForSite` creates a new `PagesFromTemplate` with its own `buildState`, but shares the same `HandleResource` function. The `HandleResource` function creates a `resourceSource` with `rc` (the compiled `ResourceConfig`). 

But wait - the `rc` is compiled once when `HandleResource` is first called. If there are multiple sites, each clone calls `HandleResource` separately, and each call compiles `rc` again. Since `rc` is a pointer, this could be a race condition if multiple sites process the same template concurrently.

But actually, looking at the code more carefully in `content_map.go`:

```go
HandleResource: func(pt *pagesfromdata.PagesFromTemplate, rc *pagemeta.ResourceConfig) error {
    s := pt.Site.(*Site)
    if err := rc.Compile(
        pt.GoTmplFi.Meta().PathInfo.Base(),
        pt.GoTmplFi,
        s.Conf,
        s.conf.MediaTypes.Config,
    ); err != nil {
        return err
    }
    rs := &resourceSource{path: rc.PathInfo, rc: rc, opener: nil, fi: pt.GoTmplFi, sv: s.siteVector}
    _, n, updated := s.pageMap.treeResources.InsertWithLock(rs.path.Base(), rs)
    ...
}
```

The `rc` is the same pointer for all sites! It's passed from `AddResource`:

```go
func (p *pagesFromDataTemplateContext) AddResource(v any) (string, error) {
    ...
    var rd pagemeta.ResourceConfig
    if err := mapstructure.WeakDecode(m, &rd); err != nil {
        return "", err
    }
    rd.ContentAdapterSourceEntryHash = hash
    ...
    return "", p.p.HandleResource(p.p, &rd)
}
```

So `rd` is a local variable in `AddResource`. Its address is passed to `HandleResource`. But `AddResource` is called ONCE (not per site), and then `HandleResource` is called for each site. Wait, let me check this again.

Actually, looking at the execution flow: The template is executed once, which calls `AddResource` once. `AddResource` creates a `ResourceConfig` on the stack and passes its address to `HandleResource`. `HandleResource` compiles it and inserts it into the page map.

For multiple sites, `CloneForSite` is called, but this doesn't re-execute the template. Instead, the `resourceSource` is cloned (via `clone()`) for each site. Let me check how this works...

Actually, let me look at `content_map.go` more carefully:

2026-05-29 21:49:10,208 - INFO - swea-agent-gohugoio__hugo-14685 - 💭 THOUGHT
Interesting! In `cloneWithUpdates`, line 611-614, when content is updated, a NEW closure is created that creates a NEW `ReadSeekCloser` every time:

```go
r.sd.OpenReadSeekCloser = func() (hugio.ReadSeekCloser, error) {
    return hugio.NewReadSeekerNoOpCloserFromString(*u.content), nil
}
```

This is the correct pattern - each call to the closure creates a new reader from the string. But compare this with `ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser`:

```go
func (s Source) ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser() hugio.OpenReadSeekCloser {
    return hugio.NewOpenReadSeekCloser(hugio.NewReadSeekerNoOpCloserFromString(s.ValueAsString()))
}
```

And `NewOpenReadSeekCloser`:
```go
func NewOpenReadSeekCloser(r ReadSeekCloser) OpenReadSeekCloser {
    return func() (ReadSeekCloser, error) {
        r.Seek(0, io.SeekStart)
        return r, nil
    }
}
```

This creates the `ReadSeekCloser` ONCE (the `r` parameter), and then the closure seeks it back to 0 and returns the SAME instance every time. This is the problematic pattern!

If two goroutines call this closure concurrently:
1. Goroutine A calls, gets `r`, starts reading
2. Goroutine B calls, calls `r.Seek(0, io.SeekStart)` while A is still reading
3. A gets corrupted data

The fix should be to create a new reader each time, like in `cloneWithUpdates`. The pattern should be:

```go
func (s Source) ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser() hugio.OpenReadSeekCloser {
    content := s.ValueAsString()
    return func() (hugio.ReadSeekCloser, error) {
        return hugio.NewReadSeekerNoOpCloserFromString(content), nil
    }
}
```

But wait, there's another thing to consider. Let me check if `ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser` is called multiple times or just once.

Looking at the call sites:
1. `content_map_page_assembler.go:1233`: `rd.OpenReadSeekCloser = rc.Content.ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser()` - called once per resource
2. `page__meta.go:352`: `openSource: pc.Content.ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser(),` - called once per page

Each call creates a new closure. But if `ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser` is called multiple times for the same `Source`, each call creates a new closure with a new `ReadSeekCloser`. However, if the same closure is used by multiple goroutines (which is possible if the resource is used concurrently), then we have the race condition.

Actually, looking more carefully: `ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser` is called ONCE in the assembler, and the resulting closure is stored in `rd.OpenReadSeekCloser`. That closure is then stored in `genericResource.sd.OpenReadSeekCloser`. When someone calls `ReadSeekCloser()` on the generic resource, it calls the closure, which seeks and returns the same reader.

But here's the key: each resource gets its own closure from a separate call to `ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser`. So different resources don't share the same reader. However, the SAME resource could be read concurrently by different goroutines (e.g., one for hashing, one for content rendering, one for image processing).

For a page resource that is an image, the flow could be:
1. The resource is created (with the closure)
2. The page is rendered - the resource's `.Content` might be called, which reads from the reader
3. The image is resized - `DecodeImage` reads from the reader
4. The image hash is calculated - `hash()` reads from the reader

If steps 2, 3, and 4 happen concurrently, they all call `ReadSeekCloser()` which calls the same closure, which seeks the same reader to 0 and returns it. This is the race!

Now, `strings.NewReader` is actually safe for concurrent use (it doesn't have any mutable state other than the read position). But the `Seek` call in the closure is the problem: one goroutine could be reading while another calls `Seek(0)`, resetting the position.

Let me verify this by looking at how `hash()` is called and if there's any concurrent access:

Looking at `resourceHash.init`:
```go
func (r *resourceHash) init(l hugio.ReadSeekCloserProvider) error {
    var initErr error
    r.initOnce.Do(func() {
        ...
        f, err := l.ReadSeekCloser()
        ...
    })
    return initErr
}
```

This uses `sync.Once`, so it's safe. But the `ReadSeekCloser` call inside the `Once` still calls the shared closure.

For `DecodeImage`:
```go
func (i *imageResource) DecodeImage() (image.Image, error) {
    f, err := i.ReadSeekCloser()
    if err != nil {
        return nil, fmt.Errorf("failed to open image for decode: %w", err)
    }
    defer f.Close()
    return i.getSpec().Imaging.Codec.DecodeFormat(i.Format, f)
}
```

And `Content`:
```go
func (l *genericResource) Content(context.Context) (any, error) {
    r, err := l.ReadSeekCloser()
    if err != nil {
        return "", err
    }
    defer r.Close()
    return hugio.ReadString(r)
}
```

Both call `ReadSeekCloser()` which calls the closure.

Now, if the image resource is cloned for multiple sites, each clone would have its own `genericResource` but they might share the same `OpenReadSeekCloser`? Let me check `clone()`:

```go
func (l *genericResource) clone() *genericResource {
    ...
}
```

   595	        if len(in) == 0 {
   596	                return
   597	        }
   598	        if r.sd.Data == nil {
   599	                r.sd.Data = make(map[string]any)
   600	        }
   601	        for k, v := range in {
   602	                if _, found := r.sd.Data[k]; !found {
   603	                        r.sd.Data[k] = v
   604	                }
   605	        }
   606	}

Note that `clone()` returns `&l` - it returns a pointer to the original struct with only the sync primitives reset. The `sd` field is shared! So all clones share the same `ResourceSourceDescriptor`, which includes the `OpenReadSeekCloser`.

This means when a resource is cloned for multiple sites (or for any other reason), all clones share the same `OpenReadSeekCloser` closure. When multiple goroutines process these clones concurrently, they all call the same closure, which seeks and returns the same `ReadSeekCloser`. This is the race condition!

Now let me verify: when a page resource is created from a content adapter, does it get cloned?

Looking at `content_map_page_assembler.go`:
```go
rs.r = r
```

The resource `r` is created via `NewResource` or `NewResourceWrapperFromResourceConfig`. It's stored in `rs.r`. Then later, when `getResourcesForPage` is called, `rs.r` is returned:

```go
case *resourceSource:
    r := n.r
    if r == nil {
        panic(...)
    }
    res = append(res, r)
```

But I need to check if the resource is cloned when used by different pages or for different sites. Let me look at the site assembly process:

Actually, let me now focus on the fix. The problem seems to be in `ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser`:

```go
func (s Source) ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser() hugio.OpenReadSeekCloser {
    return hugio.NewOpenReadSeekCloser(hugio.NewReadSeekerNoOpCloserFromString(s.ValueAsString()))
}
```

This creates a single `ReadSeekCloser` that is reused. The fix should create a new reader each time the closure is called:

```go
func (s Source) ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser() hugio.OpenReadSeekCloser {
    content := s.ValueAsString()
    return func() (hugio.ReadSeekCloser, error) {
        return hugio.NewReadSeekerNoOpCloserFromString(content), nil
    }
}
```

But wait, there's another issue. What if `ValueAsString()` is called multiple times and the `Value` is a `resource.Resource`? Let me check:

```go
func (s Source) ValueAsString() string {
    if s.Value == nil {
        return ""
    }
    ss, err := cast.ToStringE(s.Value)
    if err != nil {
        panic(fmt.Errorf("content source: failed to convert %T to string: %s", s.Value, err))
    }
    return ss
}
```

If `s.Value` is a `resource.Resource`, `cast.ToStringE` would probably call `.String()` or something, but it might not return the actual content. Actually, `cast.ToStringE` for a `resource.Resource` might fail. Let me check...

Actually, looking at the PR description, the issue is specifically about using `.Content` value (which returns a string). But the user says "The page resource is created without error if I set `content.value` to the global resource itself", which goes through the `IsResourceValue()` path.

package main

import (
    "fmt"
    "io"
    "strings"
    "sync"
)

type ReadSeekCloser interface {
    io.ReadSeeker
    io.Closer
}

type readSeekerNopCloser struct {
    io.ReadSeeker
}

func (r readSeekerNopCloser) Close() error {
    return nil
}

type OpenReadSeekCloser func() (ReadSeekCloser, error)

func NewOpenReadSeekCloser(r ReadSeekCloser) OpenReadSeekCloser {
    return func() (ReadSeekCloser, error) {
        r.Seek(0, io.SeekStart)
        return r, nil
    }
}

func NewReadSeekerNoOpCloserFromString(content string) ReadSeekCloser {
    return readSeekerNopCloser{strings.NewReader(content)}
}

func main() {
    content := "Hello World! This is a test content."
    opener := NewOpenReadSeekCloser(NewReadSeekerNoOpCloserFromString(content))
    
    var wg sync.WaitGroup
    for i := 0; i < 100; i++ {
        wg.Add(1)
        go func() {
            defer wg.Done()
            r, _ := opener()
            defer r.Close()
            buf := make([]byte, len(content))
            n, err := io.ReadFull(r, buf)
            if err != nil {
                fmt.Printf("Error: %v\n", err)
                return
            }
            if n != len(content) {
                fmt.Printf("Short read: got %d, expected %d\n", n, len(content))
            }
            if string(buf) != content {
                fmt.Printf("Content mismatch: got %q, expected %q\n", string(buf), content)
            }
        }()
    }
    wg.Wait()
    fmt.Println("Done")
}
EOF

The other two are test files.\n\nNow, what's the best fix? The issue is that `NewOpenReadSeekCloser` creates a closure that returns the same reader. The fix should be to create a new reader each time.\n\nBut actually, `NewOpenReadSeekCloser` is a general utility function. The problem is in how it's used. The only production usage is in `page_frontmatter.go:558`. The other two are test files.

Now, what's the best fix? The issue is that `NewOpenReadSeekCloser` creates a closure that returns the same reader. The fix should be to create a new reader each time.

But actually, `NewOpenReadSeekCloser` is a general utility function. The problem is in how it's used. The function itself is fine if the caller understands that it reuses the same reader. But the callers might not realize this.

Looking at the code, `NewOpenReadSeekCloser` is documented as:
```go
// NewOpenReadSeekCloser creates a new ReadSeekCloser from the given ReadSeeker.
// The ReadSeeker will be seeked to the beginning before returned.
func NewOpenReadSeekCloser(r ReadSeekCloser) OpenReadSeekCloser {
    return func() (ReadSeekCloser, error) {
        r.Seek(0, io.SeekStart)
        return r, nil
    }
}
```

The problem is that it returns the same `r` every time. A safer approach would be to create a new reader from the underlying data. But since `ReadSeekCloser` is an interface, we can't clone it generically.

For the specific case of `stringReadSeeker`, we can read the string and create a new reader each time. But the general `NewOpenReadSeekCloser` function doesn't know the underlying type.

I think the fix should be in `ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser` to not use `NewOpenReadSeekCloser` but instead create a new reader each time:

```go
func (s Source) ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser() hugio.OpenReadSeekCloser {
    content := s.ValueAsString()
    return func() (hugio.ReadSeekCloser, error) {
        return hugio.NewReadSeekerNoOpCloserFromString(content), nil
    }
}
```

But also, I should check if `NewOpenReadSeekCloser` needs to be fixed more broadly. Let me check what other callers might have the same issue...

Actually, looking at the test files that use it, they probably don't have concurrent access issues. The production code at `page_frontmatter.go:558` is the only one that could be affected.

   240	type Options struct {
   241	        // The target path relative to the publish directory.
   242	        // Unix style path, i.e. "images/logo.png".
   243	        TargetPath string
   244	
   245	        // Whether the TargetPath has a hash in it which will change if the resource changes.
   246	        // If not, we will calculate a hash from the content.
   247	        TargetPathHasHash bool
   248	
   249	        // The content to create the Resource from.
   250	        CreateContent func() (func() (hugio.ReadSeekCloser, error), error)
   251	}
   252	
   253	// FromOpts creates a new Resource from the given Options.
   254	// Make sure to set optis.TargetPathHasHash if the TargetPath already contains a hash,
   255	// as this avoids the need to calculate it.
   256	// To create a new ReadSeekCloser from a string, use hugio.NewReadSeekerNoOpCloserFromString,
   257	// or hugio.NewReadSeekerNoOpCloserFromBytes for a byte slice.
   258	// See FromString.
   259	func (c *Client) FromOpts(opts Options) (resource.Resource, error) {
   260	        opts.TargetPath = path.Clean(opts.TargetPath)
   261	        var hash string
   262	        var newReadSeeker func() (hugio.ReadSeekCloser, error) = nil
   263	        if !opts.TargetPathHasHash {
   264	                var err error
   265	                newReadSeeker, err = opts.CreateContent()
   266	                if err != nil {
   267	                        return nil, err
   268	                }
   269	                if err := func() error {
   270	                        r, err := newReadSeeker()
   271	                        if err != nil {
   272	                                return err
   273	                        }
   274	                        defer r.Close()
   275	
   276	                        hash, err = hashing.XxHashFromReaderHexEncoded(r)
   277	                        if err != nil {
   278	                                return err
   279	                        }
   280	                        return nil
   281	                }(); err != nil {
   282	                        return nil, err
   283	                }
   284	        }
   285	
   286	        key := dynacache.CleanKey(opts.TargetPath) + hash
   287	        r, err := c.rs.ResourceCache.GetOrCreate(key, func() (resource.Resource, error) {
   288	                if newReadSeeker == nil {
   289	                        var err error
   290	                        newReadSeeker, err = opts.CreateContent()
   291	                        if err != nil {
   292	                                return nil, err
   293	                        }
   294	                }
   295	                return c.rs.NewResource(
   296	                        resources.ResourceSourceDescriptor{
   297	                                LazyPublish:   true,
   298	                                GroupIdentity: identity.Anonymous, // All usage of this resource are tracked via its string content.
   299	                                OpenReadSeekCloser: func() (hugio.ReadSeekCloser, error) {
   300	                                        return newReadSeeker()
   301	                                },
   302	                                TargetPath: opts.TargetPath,
   303	                        })
   304	        })
   305	
   306	        return r, err
   307	}
   308	
   309	// FromString creates a new Resource from a string with the given relative target path.
   310	func (c *Client) FromString(targetPath, content string) (resource.Resource, error) {
   311	        return c.FromOpts(Options{
   312	                TargetPath: targetPath,
   313	                CreateContent: func() (func() (hugio.ReadSeekCloser, error), error) {
   314	                        return func() (hugio.ReadSeekCloser, error) {
   315	                                return hugio.NewReadSeekerNoOpCloserFromString(content), nil
   316	                        }, nil
   317	                },
   318	        })
   319	}

2026-05-29 21:54:18,873 - INFO - swea-agent-gohugoio__hugo-14685 - ========================= STEP 62 =========================
2026-05-29 21:54:18,884 - DEBUG - swea-lm-gohugoio__hugo-14685 - n_cache_control: 2
2026-05-29 21:54:29,247 - DEBUG - swea-lm-gohugoio__hugo-14685 - Response: ModelResponse(id='bc7c5a1a8b7f4a779fc8c9f4d2388754', created=1780091660, model='DeepSeek-V4-Pro', object='chat.completion', system_fingerprint=None, choices=[Choices(finish_reason='tool_calls', index=0, message=Message(content='This also creates a new reader each time - safe.\n\nSo the only problematic usage was in `ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser` which I\'ve now fixed.\n\nNow let me also think about the `NewOpenReadSeekCloser` function itself. Even though it\'s only used in test files now, it could be a trap for future developers. Let me consider whether to fix it too.\n\nLooking at `NewOpenReadSeekCloser`:\n```go\nfunc NewOpenReadSeekCloser(r ReadSeekCloser) OpenReadSeekCloser {\n    return func() (ReadSeekCloser, error) {\n        r.Seek(0, io.SeekStart)\n        return r, nil\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis function fundamentally can\'t be made thread-safe without changing its signature or behavior. It takes a `ReadSeekCloser` and returns a closure that returns the same reader. To make it thread-safe, we would need to read all the content upfront and create new readers from that. So the only problematic usage was in `ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser` which I've now fixed.

Now let me also think about the `NewOpenReadSeekCloser` function itself. Even though it's only used in test files now, it could be a trap for future developers. Let me consider whether to fix it too.

Looking at `NewOpenReadSeekCloser`:
```go
func NewOpenReadSeekCloser(r ReadSeekCloser) OpenReadSeekCloser {
    return func() (ReadSeekCloser, error) {
        r.Seek(0, io.SeekStart)
        return r, nil
    }
}
```

This function fundamentally can't be made thread-safe without changing its signature or behavior. It takes a `ReadSeekCloser` and returns a closure that returns the same reader. To make it thread-safe, we would need to read all the content upfront and create new readers from that. But that changes the semantics (e.g., for large files, we'd be reading everything into memory).

Given that the only production usage was in `ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser` which I've fixed, and the function is still correct for single-threaded use cases (like tests), I'll leave it as is.

Now let me also think about whether there's a similar issue in the `ValueAsString` method when the value is a `resource.Resource`. Let me check:

```go
func (s Source) ValueAsString() string {
    if s.Value == nil {
        return ""
    }
    ss, err := cast.ToStringE(s.Value)
    ...
}
```

If `s.Value` is a `resource.Resource`, `cast.ToStringE` would try to convert it to string. This might call `.String()` on it, but that might not return the actual content. However, this path is only used when `IsResourceValue()` returns false (since if it returns true, the other path is taken). So if someone passes a resource (not string), `IsResourceValue()` returns true and we go through `NewResourceWrapperFromResourceConfig`. If someone passes `.Content` (a string), `IsResourceValue()` returns false and we go through the string path.

But wait, what if someone passes a resource that implements `resource.Resource` but the `IsResourceValue` check fails? Let me look at the check:

```go
func (s Source) IsResourceValue() bool {
    _, ok := s.Value.(resource.Resource)
    return ok
}
```

This checks if `s.Value` implements `resource.Resource`. If someone passes a global resource directly, this returns true. If someone passes the `.Content` of a resource (which is a string), this returns false.

cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/test_fix.go << 'EOF'
package main

import (
    "fmt"
    "io"
    "strings"
    "sync"
)

type ReadSeekCloser interface {
    io.ReadSeeker
    io.Closer
}

type readSeekerNopCloser struct {
    io.ReadSeeker
}

func (r readSeekerNopCloser) Close() error {
    return nil
}

type OpenReadSeekCloser func() (ReadSeekCloser, error)

// Old buggy implementation
func NewOpenReadSeekCloserOld(r ReadSeekCloser) OpenReadSeekCloser {
    return func() (ReadSeekCloser, error) {
        r.Seek(0, io.SeekStart)
        return r, nil
    }
}

func NewReadSeekerNoOpCloserFromString(content string) ReadSeekCloser {
    return readSeekerNopCloser{strings.NewReader(content)}
}

// New fixed implementation
func ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloserFixed(content string) OpenReadSeekCloser {
    return func() (ReadSeekCloser, error) {
        return NewReadSeekerNoOpCloserFromString(content), nil
    }
}

func test(name string, opener OpenReadSeekCloser, content string) {
    var wg sync.WaitGroup
    errors := 0
    var mu sync.Mutex
    
    for i := 0; i < 100; i++ {
        wg.Add(1)
        go func() {
            defer wg.Done()
            r, err := opener()
            if err != nil {
                mu.Lock()
                errors++
                mu.Unlock()
                return
            }
            defer r.Close()
            buf := make([]byte, len(content))
            n, err := io.ReadFull(r, buf)
            if err != nil {
                mu.Lock()
                errors++
                mu.Unlock()
                return
            }
            if n != len(content) {
                mu.Lock()
                errors++
                mu.Unlock()
            }
            if string(buf) != content {
                mu.Lock()
                errors++
                mu.Unlock()
            }
        }()
    }
    wg.Wait()
    
    if errors > 0 {
        fmt.Printf("%s: FAILED with %d errors\n", name, errors)
    } else {
        fmt.Printf("%s: PASSED\n", name)
    }
}

func main() {
    content := "Hello World! This is a test content that is long enough to potentially cause race conditions when multiple goroutines read concurrently."
    
    oldOpener := NewOpenReadSeekCloserOld(NewReadSeekerNoOpCloserFromString(content))
    test("Old (buggy)", oldOpener, content)
    
    newOpener := ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloserFixed(content)
    test("New (fixed)", newOpener, content)
}
EOF

Actually, let me check if there's a way the `NewOpenReadSeekCloser` could be fixed too. The issue is that it reuses the same reader. The alternative is to read all content upfront:

```go
func NewOpenReadSeekCloser(r ReadSeekCloser) OpenReadSeekCloser {
    // Read all content to allow safe concurrent access.
    b, err := io.ReadAll(r)
    if err != nil {
        return func() (ReadSeekCloser, error) {
            return nil, err
        }
    }
    return func() (ReadSeekCloser, error) {
        return NewReadSeekerNoOpCloserFromBytes(b), nil
    }
}
```

But this changes the semantics: it reads everything into memory, which might not be desired for large files. Also, this function is used in tests where the old behavior (seek to 0) is expected.

When multiple goroutines concurrently read from this shared reader (e.g., for hashing, content rendering, and image resizing), one goroutine could call `Seek(0, io.SeekStart)` while another was still reading, causing corrupted/incomplete data and intermittent errors like "invalid JPEG format: short Huffman data".\n\n## Changes Made:\n\n1. **Fixed `resources/page/pagemeta/page_frontmatter.go` - `ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser()` method**:\n   - Changed from reusing a single `ReadSeekCloser` instance to creating a fresh reader on each call\n   - Captures the content string once and returns a closure that creates new `ReadSeekerNoOpCloserFromString` readers each time\n   - This ensures each concurrent read gets its own independent reader, eliminating the race condition\n\n## Key Features:\n- ✅ Eliminates race condition in concurrent resource reading\n- ✅ Maintains backward compatibility - all existing functionality preserved\n- ✅ No performance impact for single-threaded use cases\n- ✅ Consistent with other code patterns in the codebase (e.g., `cloneWithUpdates`)\n- ✅ All existing tests continue to pass\n\nThe fix ensures that page resources created from global resources\' `.Content` values work reliably, regardless of concurrent access patterns.', role='assistant', tool_calls=None, function_call=None, provider_specific_fields={'refusal': None}), provider_specific_fields={'content_filter_results': {}})], usage=Usage(completion_tokens=733, prompt_tokens=93186, total_tokens=93919, completion_tokens_details=None, prompt_tokens_details=None, audio_prompt_tokens=0), service_tier=None, prompt_filter_results=None)

Seeks the **same** `ReadSeekCloser` instance back to position 0\n2. Returns that same instance\n\nWhen multiple goroutines tried to read from the resource concurrently (e.g., one goroutine computing the hash, another rendering content, another resizing the image), they all called the closure which returned the same underlying `strings.Reader`. One goroutine could be in the middle of reading while another called `Seek(0)`, causing the first goroutine to read corrupted/incomplete data. This resulted in errors like "invalid JPEG format: short Huffman data".\n\n### Fix\n\nChanged `ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser()` to create a **new** `ReadSeekCloser` from the string content each time the closure is called, following the same safe pattern used in `genericResource.cloneWithUpdates()`:\n\n```go\nfunc (s Source) ValueAsOpenReadSeekCloser() hugio.OpenReadSeekCloser {\n    content := s.ValueAsString()\n    return func() (hugio.ReadSeekCloser, error) {\n        return hugio.NewReadSeekerNoOpCloserFromString(content), nil\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis ensures each call creates a fresh reader, making it safe for concurrent access.', role='assistant', tool_calls=None, function_call=None, provider_specific_fields={'refusal': None}), provider_specific_fields={'content_filter_results': {}})], usage=Usage(completion_tokens=386, prompt_tokens=125354, total_tokens=125740, completion_tokens_details=None, prompt_tokens_details=None, audio_prompt_tokens=0), service_tier=None, prompt_filter_results=None)
